## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators and dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching a second-order ODE written as a first-order system for oscillatory motion. Nonlinear harmonic oscillator models commonly express dv_dt as a restoring term in x plus damping in v, optionally with nonlinearities and external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (pure restoring acceleration proportional to displacement)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (spring-mass-damper with linear drag)
- Constant + linear terms (bias/offset): dv_dt = c0 - c1 * x - c2 * v (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared damping with sign)
- Coulomb (dry) friction approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (smoothed sign(v) friction using a rational regularization)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order polynomial stiffness: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Geometric nonlinearity via sine (pendulum-like): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (restoring force periodic in angle-like displacement)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small amplitude, positive at large amplitude)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * v**2) * v (nonlinear velocity-dependent pumping/damping)
- Liénard-type form (general self-oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping with linear stiffness)
- Forced oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Forced Duffing (nonlinear + drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos-capable driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, Mathieu-like structure)
- State-dependent frequency/damping coupling: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent natural frequency and dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring symmetry: for many oscillators, dv_dt is an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x**3, -sin(c*x)), reflecting a symmetric potential about x=0.
- Conservative dynamics clue: if dv_dt depends on x only (no v, no t), the system is energy-conserving and trajectories in (x,v) form closed orbits.
- Dissipation signature: terms proportional to v (or v*Abs(v)) dissipate energy; the sign should oppose v for physical damping (negative contribution when v>0, positive when v<0).
- Amplitude-dependent stiffness: inclusion of x**3, x**5, or sin(c*x) changes the oscillation frequency with amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Self-excited limit cycles: a factor like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicates negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, producing stable periodic motion without explicit forcing.
- External forcing indicator: explicit t-only terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) inject energy and can create resonance and entrainment.
- Parametric resonance indicator: time-varying coefficients multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) suggest Mathieu-type instability tongues rather than direct forcing.
- Non-smooth friction: use of Abs(v) or a smoothed v/(Abs(v)+c) term models dry friction/velocity-squared drag, typically producing sharper waveform corners and faster decay at high speeds.
